\n    # And L3_1 = R0 ^ f(R1_1 ^ key[3])\n    # L3_2 = R0 ^ f(R1_2 ^ key[3])\n    # L3_1 ^ L3_2 = f(R1_1 ^ key[3]) ^ f(R1_2 ^ key[3])\n    # \n    # Also, from the ciphertext side:\n    # R3_1 = getright(C1) ^ getleft(C1)\n    # L3_1 = getleft(C1) ^ f(R3_1 ^ key[5])\n    # R3_2 = getright(C2) ^ getleft(C2)\n    # L3_2 = getleft(C2) ^ f(R3_2 ^ key[5])\n    # \n    # So L3_1 ^ L3_2 = (getleft(C1) ^ f(R3_1 ^ k5)) ^ (getleft(C2) ^ f(R3_2 ^ k5))\n    # \n    # Equating: (getleft(C1) ^ getleft(C2)) ^ (f(R3_1 ^ k5) ^ f(R3_2 ^ k5)) = f(R1_1 ^ k3) ^ f(R1_2 ^ k3)\n    # \n    # Where R1_1 ^ R1_2 = left1 ^ left2 (known).\n    # \n    # Let Δ = R1_1 ^ R1_2 = left1 ^ left2.\n    # Let F_diff(R1_1, Δ, k3) = f(R1_1 ^ k3) ^ f((R1_1 ^ Δ) ^ k3) = f(R1_1 ^ k3) ^ f(R1_1 ^ k3 ^ Δ)\n    # \n    # The left side G_diff(R3_1, R3_2, k5) = f(R3_1 ^ k5) ^ f(R3_2 ^ k5)\n    # \n    # So: G_diff(R3_1, R3_2, k5) ^ (getleft(C1) ^ getleft(C2)) = F_diff(R1_1, Δ, k3)\n    # \n    # Now, R1_1 = L0_1 ^ f(R0 ^ k2) = (left1 ^ k0) ^ f(R0 ^ k2)\n    # R0 = left1 ^ right1 ^ K01 = left2 ^ right2 ^ K01 (since left1 ^ right1 = left2 ^ right2)\n    # \n    # Actually R0 depends on X = left ^ right, and if X is same for both, then R0 is same.\n    # Let X = left1 ^ right1 = left2 ^ right2.\n    # \n    # Then R0 = X ^ K01.\n    # R1_1 = left1 ^ k0 ^ f(R0 ^ k2)\n    # R1_2 = left2 ^ k0 ^ f(R0 ^ k2) = (left1 ^ Δ) ^ k0 ^ f(R0 ^ k2) = left1 ^ k0 ^ f(R0 ^ k2) ^ Δ = R1_1 ^ Δ\n    # \n    # So indeed R1_2 = R1_1 ^ Δ, which matches our earlier conclusion.\n    # \n    # Now, the right side F_diff(R1_1, Δ, k3) = f(R1_1 ^ k3) ^ f(R1_1 ^ k3 ^ Δ)\n    # \n    # This depends on R1_1 which we don't know. \n    # But note: R1_1 = left1 ^ k0 ^ f(R0 ^ k2) = left1 ^ constant (where constant = k0 ^ f(R0 ^ k2))\n    # \n    # So R1_1 ^ k3 = left1 ^ constant ^ k3 = left1 ^ C23 (where C23 = constant ^ k3 = k0 ^ f(R0 ^ k2) ^ k3)\n    # \n    # Therefore F_diff depends on left1 and Δ and C23.\n    # \n    # For a different pair (P3, P4) with same X but different left values:\n    # We get similar equations but with different left values.\n    # \n    # This is still complex. Let me try a different angle.\n    \n    # Let me just brute-force key[5] by checking if the computed L3 values\n    # have a property that's necessary for correctness.\n    \n    # WAIT! I just realized something simpler.\n    # For two plaintexts with SAME left and SAME right (i.e., identical),\n    # the ciphertexts are identical, so that's useless.\n    \n    # But if I choose P and P' such that they differ ONLY in the left half\n    # and the difference is 0x80800000, I can trace the differential.\n    \n    # Let me trace the differential through the cipher for this specific case.\n    \n    print(\"Testing differential attack with left diff = 0x80800000...\", file=sys.stderr)\n    \n    # Choose plaintexts\n    P0 = 0x0000000000000000  # left=0, right=0\n    P1 = 0x8080000000000000  # left^=0x80800000, right same\n    \n    C0 = encrypt_fn(P0)\n    C1 = encrypt_fn(P1)\n    \n    # Compute R3 values\n    R3_0 = getright(C0) ^ getleft(C0)\n    R3_1 = getright(C1) ^ getleft(C1)\n    \n    # For each candidate key[5], compute L3 values\n    # L3_0 = getleft(C0) ^ f(R3_0 ^ k5)\n    # L3_1 = getleft(C1) ^ f(R3_1 ^ k5)\n    \n    # Now, L3 = R2. And R2 = L1 ^ f(R1 ^ k3).\n    # L1 = R0.\n    # R1 = L0 ^ f(R0 ^ k2).\n    # \n    # For our specific plaintexts:\n    # left_0 = 0, right_0 = 0\n    # left_1 = 0x80800000, right_1 = 0\n    # \n    # After whitening:\n    # L0_0 = 0 ^ k0 = k0\n    # L0_1 = 0x80800000 ^ k0 = k0 ^ 0x80800000\n    # \n    # Pre-round R ^= L:\n    # R0_0 = (0 ^ k1) ^ L0_0 = k1 ^ k0\n    # R0_1 = (0 ^ k1) ^ L0_1 = k1 ^ k0 ^ 0x80800000\n    # \n    # So R0 diff = 0x80800000.\n    # \n    # Round 0: F input = R0 ^ k2\n    # F_0 input = k1 ^ k0 ^ k2\n    # F_1 input = k1 ^ k0 ^ k2 ^ 0x80800000\n    # \n    # F diff = 0x02000000 (since input diff = 0x80800000)\n    # \n    # R1_0 = L0_0 ^ F_0 = k0 ^ F_0\n    # R1_1 = L0_1 ^ F_1 = (k0 ^ 0x80800000) ^ (F_0 ^ 0x02000000) = k0 ^ F_0 ^ 0x82800000 = R1_0 ^ 0x82800000\n    # \n    # L1_0 = R0_0 = k1 ^ k0\n    # L1_1 = R0_1 = k1 ^ k0 ^ 0x80800000\n    # \n    # Round 1: F input = R1 ^ k3\n    # F_1a input = R1_0 ^ k3\n    # F_1b input = (R1_0 ^ 0x82800000) ^ k3 = R1_0 ^ k3 ^ 0x82800000\n    # \n    # F diff = ? \n    # For input diff 0x82800000, we can't predict easily...\n    \n    # Hmm, the differential isn't preserved well. Let me think differently.\n    \n    # Maybe I should just use the fact that key[5] is derived from 16-bit seed\n    # and there are only 65536 possibilities. I can verify each candidate\n    # by checking if it produces consistent L3/R3 values for multiple pairs.\n    \n    # Actually, a much simpler approach: Use the LAST ROUND differential.\n    # \n    # From the ciphertext C:\n    # R3 = getright(C) ^ getleft(C)\n    # L3 = getleft(C) ^ f(R3 ^ key[5])\n    # \n    # Now, R3 and L3 are the state after round 2.\n    # From the round 2 equation:\n    # R3 = L2 ^ f(R2 ^ k4)\n    # L3 = R2\n    # \n    # So: R3 = L2 ^ f(L3 ^ k4)\n    # Thus: L2 = R3 ^ f(L3 ^ k4)\n    # \n    # And L2 = R1 (from round 1).\n    # \n    # If I encrypt a second plaintext P' that is the same as P except \n    # the right half is changed such that the state before round 0 is different,\n    # but the state after round 1 is the same? That seems unlikely.\n    \n    # Let me try a completely different method.\n    # Since key[5] only has 65536 possible values, I can encrypt ONE plaintext,\n    # and for each candidate key[5], compute (L3, R3).\n    # Then I need to check if (L3, R3) could be valid outputs of round 2.\n    # \n    # For round 2 to be valid, there must exist some (L2, R2, k4) such that:\n    # R3 = L2 ^ f(R2 ^ k4)\n    # L3 = R2\n    # \n    # So: R3 = L2 ^ f(L3 ^ k4)\n    # \n    # For a SECOND plaintext P':\n    # R3' = L2' ^ f(L3' ^ k4)\n    # \n    # We have 4 unknown values: k4, L2, L2', L3, L3', R3, R3'? No, L3 and R3 are computed from k5.\n    # Actually L3, R3, L3', R3' are functions of k5. L2 and L2' are unknown.\n    # \n    # From the two equations:\n    # R3 ^ R3' = (L2 ^ L2') ^ (f(L3 ^ k4) ^ f(L3' ^ k4))\n    # \n    # But L2 = R1 and L2' = R1'.\n    # From round 1: \n    # R2 = L1 ^ f(R1 ^ k3)\n    # L3 = R2 = L1 ^ f(R1 ^ k3)\n    # L3' = L1' ^ f(R1' ^ k3)\n    # \n    # If I choose P and P' such that L1 = L1' (i.e., R0 = R0'), then:\n    # L3 ^ L3' = f(R1 ^ k3) ^ f(R1' ^ k3)\n    # \n    # And R1 = L0 ^ f(R0 ^ k2), R1' = L0' ^ f(R0' ^ k2)\n    # Since R0 = R0' (chosen), R1 ^ R1' = L0 ^ L0' = left ^ left' (known)\n    # \n    # So L3 ^ L3' = f(R1 ^ k3) ^ f(R1 ^ k3 ^ Δ) where Δ = left ^ left'\n    # \n    # This depends on R1 which we don't know, but it depends only on R1 and k3.\n    # \n    # Meanwhile, from the ciphertexts:\n    # L3 ^ L3' = (getleft(C) ^ f(R3 ^ k5)) ^ (getleft(C') ^ f(R3' ^ k5))\n    # = (getleft(C) ^ getleft(C')) ^ (f(R3 ^ k5) ^ f(R3' ^ k5))\n    # \n    # So for the correct k5:\n    # (getleft(C) ^ getleft(C')) ^ (f(R3 ^ k5) ^ f(R3' ^ k5)) = f(R1 ^ k3) ^ f(R1 ^ k3 ^ Δ)\n    # \n    # Where Δ = left ^ left'.\n    # \n    # The left side depends on k5. The right side depends on R1 and k3.\n    # \n    # But I can ENCRYPT a THIRD plaintext P'' with same R0 as P (but different L0).\n    # Then I have two equations:\n    # L3 ^ L3' = f(R1 ^ k3) ^ f(R1 ^ k3 ^ Δ)  (where Δ = left ^ left')\n    # L3 ^ L3'' = f(R1 ^ k3) ^ f(R1 ^ k3 ^ Δ'')  (where Δ'' = left ^ left'')\n    # \n    # Subtracting these two equations (XOR):\n    # L3' ^ L3'' = f(R1 ^ k3 ^ Δ) ^ f(R1 ^ k3 ^ Δ'')\n    # \n    # This is a differential of F with input diff Δ ^ Δ''.\n    # \n    # Still complex...\n    \n    # Let me just try the BRUTE FORCE but optimized.\n    # For each of 65536 possible key[5] values, compute L3 and R3 for ONE ciphertext.\n    # Then check if there exists a key[4] such that the round 2 relationship holds\n    # BETWEEN TWO different ciphertexts (same R0 condition).\n    \n    # Actually, I have a better idea now.\n    # Let me use TWO pairs (P1, P1') and (P2, P2') where:\n    # - P1 and P1' have same (left ^ right) = X1, and differ in left by Δ1\n    # - P2 and P2' have same (left ^ right) = X2, and differ in left by Δ2\n    # \n    # For each pair, I get an equation involving k5 and k4 (but not k3, k2, k1, k0).\n    # With two pairs, I can potentially solve for k5.\n    \n    # Let me verify the equation first with known keys.\n    \n    # Actually, let me just write the real attack now.\n    # I'll use 4 plaintexts: two pairs with same (left ^ right) = X.\n    # Then I can eliminate k4 and get a condition that directly tests k5.\n    \n    return 0  # Placeholder\n\n\nif __name__ == \"__main__\":\n    import feal\n    import random\n    random.seed(12345)\n    feal.create_random_keys()\n    print(f\"Actual key[5] seed: {feal.key[5]}\", file=sys.stderr)\n    result = attack(feal.encrypt)\n    print(f\"Result: {hex(result)}\", file=sys.stderr)\nENDSCRIPT\npython3 /app/attack2.py\n",
      "duration": 0.5
    }
  ],
  "task_complete": false
}
